  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8a85e9bd-5db6-452f-b332-976613e8e8ee'
      });
    }

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1103695282" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1103695282" />
    <a title="Glenn Russell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23385697-glenn-russell"><img alt="Glenn Russell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505195595p2/23385697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1103695282?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Glenn Russell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Glenn Russell" href="/user/show/23385697-glenn-russell">Glenn Russell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23385697-glenn-russell?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1103695282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10279994457789313245"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466532667i/19491280._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>CORONAVIRUS UPDATE - In light of our current crisis, many embraces are needed. Of course, as we all recognize, social distancing prevents our physical embraces but now is the time for a mental embrace of our entire human family. <br/><br/>Eduardo Galeano of Uruguay (1940-2015) is one of the finest of the Latin American writers. If you would like to add a healthy dose of inspiration and magic in your life, pick up <i>The Book of Embraces</i>, a collection of over 200 poetic memoirs/stories/happenings complete wit</span>
  <span id="freeText10279994457789313245" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466532667i/19491280._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>CORONAVIRUS UPDATE - In light of our current crisis, many embraces are needed. Of course, as we all recognize, social distancing prevents our physical embraces but now is the time for a mental embrace of our entire human family. <br><br>Eduardo Galeano of Uruguay (1940-2015) is one of the finest of the Latin American writers. If you would like to add a healthy dose of inspiration and magic in your life, pick up <i>The Book of Embraces</i>, a collection of over 200 poetic memoirs/stories/happenings complete with the author's fanciful montage images covering a range of topics: art, dreams, the human voice, names, Indians, television, the culture of terror, to name several. To share a taste of this literary fiesta, here are my brief comments coupled with the author’s quotes.<br><br>THE FUNCTION OF ART<br>“Diego had never seen the sea. His father took him to discover it. . . . And so immense was the sea and its sparkle that the child was struck dumb by the beauty of it. And when he finally managed to speak, trembling, stuttering, he asked his father: “Help me to see!”” --------- As in nature, so in art. As a young boy growing up in the country I was infatuated with the drawings I saw in books of knights in armor. My parents brought me to the Metropolitan Museum in New York City where I walked into a room with an entire exhibit of knights in armor on horses surrounded by colorful banners. I was likewise struck dumb. <br><br>GRAPES AND WINE<br>“On his deathbed, a man of the vineyards spoke into Marcela’s ear. Before dying, he revealed his secret: “The grape,” he whispered, “is made of wine.” Marcela Perez-Silva told me this, and I thought: If the grape is made of wine, then perhaps we are the words that tell who we are.” ---------- Bulls-eye, Eduardo. The notion that humans are rational animals is sheer poppycock. I’m rarely rational and usually not in my best moments. We humans are word-symbol-language making animals.<br><br>THE FUNCTION OF A READER<br>“When Lucia Palaez was very small, she read a novel under the covers. She read it in fragments, night after night, hiding it under the pillow. She had stolen it from the cedar bookshelf where her uncle kept his favorite books. . . . Lucia has never read that book again. She would no longer recognize it. It has grown so much inside her that now it is something else: now it is hers. ---------- I recently read where a young man insisted an attractive young lady date him. The mademoiselle asked him, in turn: What book are you from? ----- Ha! I can’t imagine a more telling question. You are what you read. <br><br>A DEFINITION OF ART<br>Edwardo Galeano tells us of Portinari, a well-known artist in Brazil who was pressed by the communist government to give a definition of art. “I don’t know,” said Portinari. And then: “All I know is this: art is art, or it’s shit.”” ---------- After giving our time and energy to viewing much art, there comes a point where we have a very good sense of what is genuine and what is not, a point where we can trust our eyes. This reminds me of the Supreme Court Justice who said he couldn’t define hard-core pornography but knows it when he sees it. <br><br>CELEBRATION OF FANTASY<br>Galeano tells of his visit to Cuzco, Peru when a small boys crowded round him and started shouting. He writes, “Then, in the middle of this racket, a little waif who barely cleared a yard off the ground showed me a watch drawn in black ink on his wrist. “An uncle of mine who lives in Lima sent it to me,” he said. “And does it keep good time?” I asked him. “It’s a bit slow,” he admitted.” ---------- Thanks for playing the game of imagination and fantasy with a child, Eduardo! Nearly all of us have a childhood story of our artwork or creativity being putdown by a teacher, parent or other adult. Yet, when as children we conformed to established regimentation we were never putdown; quite the contrary, we were praised. <br><br>HUNGER<br>“A system of isolation: Look out for number one. Your neighbor is neither your brother nor your lover. Your neighbor is a competitor, an enemy, an obstacle to clear or an object to use. The system feeds neither the body nor the heart: many are condemned to starve for lack of bread and many more for lack of embraces. ---------- For a number of years I was part of an improvisational dance group where a few dozen dancers, mostly strangers to one another, would arrive at a designated dance space on Friday nights and dance wildly, joyfully for hours, punctuated by many tender embraces. After one session someone asked me how we can actually get away with all this on Friday nights. Sorry to say, the filmmakers who make ultra-violent movies never have to ask how they can get away with making such films. <br><br>TELEVISION<br>“Television, that final light that saves you from loneliness and from the night, is reality. Because life is a show, the system promises those who behave themselves a comfortable seat.” ---------- When I was a boy growing up in a small house the television was always on at high volume, morning, noon and night. My only escape was going off to college -- my first taste of what in India is termed moksha, that is, release from the world of ordinary experience. It’s been nearly five decades since my escape and in all those years I’ve never watched another television show. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466532221i/19491245._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="10279994457789313245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1004647394" />
    <a title="Stacia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3917029-stacia"><img alt="Stacia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316011190p2/3917029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1004647394?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia" href="/user/show/3917029-stacia">Stacia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780393029604" href="/book/show/382642.The_Book_of_Embraces">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Stacia by: </span>
      <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://electricliterature.com/a-novel-for-every-remaining-world-cup-team/">http://electricliterature.com/a-novel...</a> 
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3917029-stacia?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3917029-stacia?shelf=book-covers-i-love">book-covers-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3917029-stacia?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3917029-stacia?shelf=latin-america">latin-america</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3917029-stacia?shelf=racism-tyranny-social-justice-etc">racism-tyranny-social-justice-etc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1004647394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6247821272824674189">In a way, I find Galeano's work like Kurt Vonnegut's in that both write in a manner that comes across as deceptively simple, quick & easy to read, but then you realize that it's so tightly edited, so finely tuned, that just a few words are as accurate & as powerful as a bullet between the eyes. Galeano's wide net of musings range from friendships, to art, to dreams, to politics, to society, to heartbreaking realities of poverty, racism, war, & violence. As with many Latin American writers, there</span>
  <span id="freeText6247821272824674189" style="display:none">In a way, I find Galeano's work like Kurt Vonnegut's in that both write in a manner that comes across as deceptively simple, quick &amp; easy to read, but then you realize that it's so tightly edited, so finely tuned, that just a few words are as accurate &amp; as powerful as a bullet between the eyes. Galeano's wide net of musings range from friendships, to art, to dreams, to politics, to society, to heartbreaking realities of poverty, racism, war, &amp; violence. As with many Latin American writers, there are elements of magical realism that seem to float through some of his work. (Do the Muses give the Latin American writers some special spark?) It's almost like a collection of poetry or (very) short stories. But... not quite. Most items are maybe a paragraph or two, certainly less than a page, interspersed with some wild &amp; strange line drawings. It's not quite poetry, not quite short stories, not quite a memoir -- it is its own original creation &amp; a lovely one at that. So glad that I stumbled onto this Uruguayan gem of literature. Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6247821272824674189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Galeano is one of those writers that makes me feel like anything is possible -- write what you like, what helps you tell the most truthful version of what you want to tell, and don't care about any of the rules. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9477398831175273107">Accompanied by Galeano’s illustrations, the series of vignettes use fable, historical anecdotes, and dreamy ruminations to explore abstractions so broad they seem impossible to hold in our heads. That is until Galeano represents them (issues like “Hunger” and “The Limits of Art”) in a moment, image, or sentence with striking clarity. In “Prophecies/2,” Galeano writes, “Helena dreamed about the keepers of the fire. The poorest old women had stored it away in suburban kitchens and had only to blow</span>
  <span id="freeText9477398831175273107" style="display:none">Accompanied by Galeano’s illustrations, the series of vignettes use fable, historical anecdotes, and dreamy ruminations to explore abstractions so broad they seem impossible to hold in our heads. That is until Galeano represents them (issues like “Hunger” and “The Limits of Art”) in a moment, image, or sentence with striking clarity. In “Prophecies/2,” Galeano writes, “Helena dreamed about the keepers of the fire. The poorest old women had stored it away in suburban kitchens and had only to blow very gently on their palms to rekindle the flame.”<br /><br />–Connie Pan<br /><br /><br />from Buy, Borrow, Bypass: Books by Virgos: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bookriot.com/2017/08/28/books-by-virgos/">https://bookriot.com/2017/08/28/books...</a> </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16034255978323066106">This is a startling simple little book of vignettes about a range of subjects. The writing is very poetic and sometimes unexpectedly poignant. The kind of thing where you start a chapter about some commonplace thing and find yourself a little choked up by the end of it. Well written and one of the few books I often recommend that I would call uplifting. </span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17564041603833944482">I thank the person who recommended this to me and, when I forgot about it, recommended it to me again. I loved this book. It’s a collection of very short reflections that approach prose poetry: memories, dreams, and musings by an author I’d never heard of. Galeano is obviously well known at least in South America. He’s exiled to Barcelona for many years for political reasons I don’t pretend to understand, but returns to Uruguay near the end of his life. My ignorance of the circumstances and his </span>
  <span id="freeText17564041603833944482" style="display:none">I thank the person who recommended this to me and, when I forgot about it, recommended it to me again. I loved this book. It’s a collection of very short reflections that approach prose poetry: memories, dreams, and musings by an author I’d never heard of. Galeano is obviously well known at least in South America. He’s exiled to Barcelona for many years for political reasons I don’t pretend to understand, but returns to Uruguay near the end of his life. My ignorance of the circumstances and his other work didn’t interfere at all with my enjoyment of this wonderful book, which I’d recommend to anyone who likes magical anecdotes and tangents and doesn’t need a plot. <br /><br />In addition to the writing, Galeano is also an excellent artist and provided the witty and surreal drawings for the book. They make the book more personal, besides being quite well done. I don’t understand why the publisher decided to use folksy wooden bird carvings on the cover when there are ample - and much better - artworks to choose from from Galeano’s own hand. <br /><br />Anyway, original, poetic, transporting, and often spine-tinglingly touching passages with the occasional spritz of magical realism. Even the dedication to the translator was a knock-out. Here’s one of my favorite passages:<br /><br /><b>Grapes and Wine</b><br /><br />On his deathbed, a man of the vineyards spoke into Marcela’s ear. Before dying, he revealed his secret:<br /><br />“The grape,” he whispered, “is made of wine.” <br /><br />Marcela Perez-Silva told me this, and I thought: if the grape is made of wine, then perhaps we are the words that tell who we are.<br />*<br /><br />Much enjoyed. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17564041603833944482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14007691435468622763">I chose to read Eduardo Galeano's wonderful short stories and thoughts on a recent eight hour flight. A perfect choice! It is written in an unusually free manner, on separate pages with surreal sketches. I must have shown my enthusiasm somewhat, as one of the attendants came up to me and commented on how much she had enjoyed his work too! Brilliant comparisons, serious thoughts, a great sense of humor and a celebration of his life is found in an inspiring choice of words.<br/>I was surprised to find </span>
  <span id="freeText14007691435468622763" style="display:none">I chose to read Eduardo Galeano's wonderful short stories and thoughts on a recent eight hour flight. A perfect choice! It is written in an unusually free manner, on separate pages with surreal sketches. I must have shown my enthusiasm somewhat, as one of the attendants came up to me and commented on how much she had enjoyed his work too! Brilliant comparisons, serious thoughts, a great sense of humor and a celebration of his life is found in an inspiring choice of words.<br />I was surprised to find some discussion on the environmental problems in Canada ( "The Kingdom of the Cockroach" p.136). Here you can find a reference to the planet being abdicated in favor of the cockroaches.<br />On p. 111, you can find a reference to a book he has been reading on perfect happiness. Herein "the great grandfather is completely senile ("his thoughts are like the color of water") and displays the same beatific smile as his newly born great grandson. His great grandson is happy because he doesn't yet have any memory." But Galeano wants no part of it!<br />Eduardo claims he is the master of nothing, master of no one, not even of his own convictions. "I am my face in the wind, against the wind, and I am the wind that strikes my face."<br />On the topic of hunger, he twists his words, "Look out for number one... many are condemned to starve for lack of bread and many more for lack of embraces." (which feed the body and the heart. )<br /><br />What a great book to read and re-read! <br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1050449032" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13565954414401961039">Exile, and the end of exile, on many levels, is a central theme in The Book of Embraces, a work composed of intimate vignettes from the life of the author and the lives of many people whose stories he renders with the equal intimacy and awe. The stories may be equal parts beautiful and painful, illuminating moments that are ordinary or magical, violent or tender, humorous or tragic, but woven together so that none of the qualities can be separated from the others. It is exile, and the end of exi</span>
  <span id="freeText13565954414401961039" style="display:none">Exile, and the end of exile, on many levels, is a central theme in The Book of Embraces, a work composed of intimate vignettes from the life of the author and the lives of many people whose stories he renders with the equal intimacy and awe. The stories may be equal parts beautiful and painful, illuminating moments that are ordinary or magical, violent or tender, humorous or tragic, but woven together so that none of the qualities can be separated from the others. It is exile, and the end of exile, and when you read a book like this it leaves you naked, so that you are defenseless before all of it, and so that you laugh at your own image. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13565954414401961039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_125696107" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125696107" />
    <a title="Ruth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/316631-ruth"><img alt="Ruth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1204062236p2/316631.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125696107?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ruth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ruth" href="/user/show/316631-ruth">Ruth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125696107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13313935381889900706">This is a book of little political/personal/regional stories (actually they feel more like prose poems) side-by-side with these crazy recurring and transmuting illustrations that kind of make their own visual stories (I like the one of a cow looking up at some insects that are actually tiny helicopters & planes) about life and culture in the Americas. The titles vary from The Function of Art to The Culture of Terror to The Air and the Wind. You can just pick it up and read one or two of them and</span>
  <span id="freeText13313935381889900706" style="display:none">This is a book of little political/personal/regional stories (actually they feel more like prose poems) side-by-side with these crazy recurring and transmuting illustrations that kind of make their own visual stories (I like the one of a cow looking up at some insects that are actually tiny helicopters &amp; planes) about life and culture in the Americas. The titles vary from The Function of Art to The Culture of Terror to The Air and the Wind. You can just pick it up and read one or two of them and get knocked down by how sweet/sad/true they are. For example, the story called Celebration of the Marriage of Heart and Mind goes "Why does not one write, if not to put one's pieces together? From the moment we enter school or church, education chops up into pieces; it teaches us to divorce soul from body &amp; mind from heart. The fisherman of the Colombian coast must be learned doctors of ethics &amp; morality, for they invented the word sentipensante, feeling-thinking, to define language that speaks the truth." The whole book is like this, b/c you read/see it in these fragments, but they all fit together and echo each other to make this whole picture of the truth of what it means to be alive at this place and this time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13313935381889900706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2133873994?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34988910-patrick?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34988910-patrick?shelf=hispanic">hispanic</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2133873994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12430174995848625288">Moving collection of short stories set all across the Americas. The stories start out more abstract but slowly move towards more identifiable moments and anecdotes, until by the end they take a surprising turn into the intimate details of the life of Galeano and his friends and family. I've never read a book that involves such a subtle transition from an anonymous narrator to a partner in a dialogue -- by the end Galeano feels like an old friend, with nothing held back, the layers of artifice st</span>
  <span id="freeText12430174995848625288" style="display:none">Moving collection of short stories set all across the Americas. The stories start out more abstract but slowly move towards more identifiable moments and anecdotes, until by the end they take a surprising turn into the intimate details of the life of Galeano and his friends and family. I've never read a book that involves such a subtle transition from an anonymous narrator to a partner in a dialogue -- by the end Galeano feels like an old friend, with nothing held back, the layers of artifice stripped away until, as he says, it's just his face and the wind that blows against it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12430174995848625288" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2630733908" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2630733908" />
    <a title="Nuri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24205238-nuri"><img alt="Nuri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602277514p2/24205238.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2630733908?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nuri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nuri" href="/user/show/24205238-nuri">Nuri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24205238-nuri?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24205238-nuri?shelf=vignettes">vignettes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2630733908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9015157963695752574">"...there was nothing bad and nothing odd about the fact that my heart had broken from so much use." <br/> — Resurrection/1<br/><br/>"I recognize myself in those who will endure..."<br/> — The Air And The Wind<br/> <br/>The Book of Embraces is a collection of vignettes, celebrating the human voice and silence, that remained triumphant throughout the nervous history of the world in the clutches of evil. <br/><br/>It's a hauntingly beautiful piece of work. <br/><br/>Since the theme throughout the book is exile, it is mostly intense, especially th</span>
  <span id="freeText9015157963695752574" style="display:none">"...there was nothing bad and nothing odd about the fact that my heart had broken from so much use." <br /> — Resurrection/1<br /><br />"I recognize myself in those who will endure..."<br /> — The Air And The Wind<br /> <br />The Book of Embraces is a collection of vignettes, celebrating the human voice and silence, that remained triumphant throughout the nervous history of the world in the clutches of evil. <br /><br />It's a hauntingly beautiful piece of work. <br /><br />Since the theme throughout the book is exile, it is mostly intense, especially the sections on "The Culture Of Terror," that speaks about the atrocities under Uruguayan and Argentinian dictatorship. And "The Celebration of Courage," to praise the fallen glory.<br /><br />Some of the tender, less intense sections include Theology, The Devourer Devoured, A Little Death. <br /><br />An excerpt from Theology —<br /><blockquote>"Lately, I admit I felt envy. Just as no one can give me orders, I know nothing of the dignity of disobedience. Nor can I know the boldness of love, which requires two. In keeping with the principle of authority, I resisted the desire to congratulate them for having suddenly grown wise in human passion.<br /><br />Then came the misunderstandings. They understood "fall" when I spoke of "flight." They thought that a sin deserved punishment if it was original. I said that those who fail to love are sinners; they understood that those who love are sinners. Where I spoke of a meadow of joy their understood a vale of tears. I said that pain was the salt that gave flavour to the human adventure; they understood that I was condemning them by granting them the glory of being mortal and a little nuts. They got everything backwards. And they believed it.<br /><br />[....] When I wake up, I am alone. I have no one to play with because the angels take me so seriously, nor have I anyone to desire. I am condemned to desire myself. I wander from star to star, growing bored in the empty universe. I feel very tired, I feel very alone. I am alone alone for all eternity."</blockquote><br />The ones on rumination includes Dazed Days, Forgetting, The Fiesta.<br /><br />In Divorces, A Consumer Civilization, The System are hard hitting truths. <br /><br />Some of the most unusually beautiful sections, on the raw beauty of expression and the challenge of humanity are included Paradoxes, Alienation, Jealousy From On High, Art and Time, A Profession of Faith, Weeping, The Delivery, The Diginity of Art.<br /><br />It's a book you might find yourself going back to, more than once.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9015157963695752574" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1903584769" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1903584769" />
    <a title="Kevin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6599606-kevin"><img alt="Kevin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472211753p2/6599606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1903584769?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kevin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kevin" href="/user/show/6599606-kevin">Kevin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1903584769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7785382874103064382">The blurb perfectly summarises this book: ‘Parable, paradox, anecdote, dream and autobiography blend into an exuberant world view and affirmation of human possibility.’<br/><br/>The embraces as referred to in the title are contact with the lives and stories of humanity; Galeano shares regurgitated (for want of a better word, reproduced?) tales from his travels, research and friendships, visceral fragments of life presented in short, barely more than a page, snippets of prose. They are like a cross between</span>
  <span id="freeText7785382874103064382" style="display:none">The blurb perfectly summarises this book: ‘Parable, paradox, anecdote, dream and autobiography blend into an exuberant world view and affirmation of human possibility.’<br /><br />The embraces as referred to in the title are contact with the lives and stories of humanity; Galeano shares regurgitated (for want of a better word, reproduced?) tales from his travels, research and friendships, visceral fragments of life presented in short, barely more than a page, snippets of prose. They are like a cross between poems and short stories as demonstrated here:<br /><br />Bureaucracy/3<br /><br />Sixto Martinez completed his military service at a Seville garrison.<br /><br />In the middle of the patio was a bench. Next to the bench, a soldier stood guard. No one knew why the bench needed guarding. They guarded it because they guarded it. Day and night, all nights and all days. And generation after generation of officers transmitted the order and the soldiers obeyed. No one doubted, no one questioned. If as such it is done, and as such always have been done, a reason there had to be.<br /><br />And like this it continued until one person, I don’t know which general or colonel, wanted to see the original order. He had to forage the archives. And after much digging, he knew. Thirty-one years, two months and four days ago, an official ordered a guard to be placed by the bench that had recently been painted so that no one happened to sit on the fresh paint.<br /><br /><br />Galeano is a masterful writer, his offering is full of astute, important and empathic observations. The stories are ones to be dipped into, somewhat fleeting but the overall impression is hugely powerful. The tone of the writing is the most uplifting I have read, ‘The Book of Embraces’ is like an atheist’s bible, both a celebration of and unifying call to those who value and love humanity. I have struggled with the score, it is beautiful and unique and one I would definitely go back to, to perhaps learn by heart the particular snippets that are the most meaningful to me. If you love humanity, you will embrace this book wholeheartedly 4/5<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7785382874103064382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9442247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6245583223018146622"> "I write for those who cannot read me: the downtrodden, the ones who have been waiting on line for centuries to get into history, who cannot read a book or afford to buy one." <br/> Eduardo Galeano is a Uruguayan journalist whose works tread the border between poetry and historical narrative. <i>The Book of Embraces</i> is composed of nearly two hundred vignettes, brief anecdotes an entire universe unto themselves.<br/> The breathtaking scope of Galeano's writing is unrivaled: he skillfully muses upon art, hist</span>
  <span id="freeText6245583223018146622" style="display:none"> "I write for those who cannot read me: the downtrodden, the ones who have been waiting on line for centuries to get into history, who cannot read a book or afford to buy one." <br /> Eduardo Galeano is a Uruguayan journalist whose works tread the border between poetry and historical narrative. <i>The Book of Embraces</i> is composed of nearly two hundred vignettes, brief anecdotes an entire universe unto themselves.<br /> The breathtaking scope of Galeano's writing is unrivaled: he skillfully muses upon art, history, politics, television, tradition, death, Latin America, laughter, graffiti, paradox, love, dreams, theology, courage, all the myriad moments that have made (and continue to make) our lives upon this planet what they are. His distinctive prose, both elegant and elegiac, has the charm to provoke laughter, the ability to engender rage, the tenderness to provoke tears, and the finesse to inspire awe.</span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy Baker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy Baker" href="/user/show/12382157-christy-baker">Christy Baker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12382157-christy-baker?shelf=meditations">meditations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12382157-christy-baker?shelf=memoir-autobiography">memoir-autobiography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12382157-christy-baker?shelf=essays">essays</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12382157-christy-baker?shelf=politics-current-affairs">politics-current-affairs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2597905292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8874391317116545556">A highly mixed blend of brief historical stories of the wars and atrocities and dictators in various Central and South American countries, bits of dream fragments, lyrical, almost poetic phrases, fable or wisdom teaching stories...a hard book to describe. I would find a few concepts that would please my ear or make me pause to reflect awhile on a lovely metaphor of wine and grapes and life and then find a stark contrast on the next page of an account of torture and execution of an artist followe</span>
  <span id="freeText8874391317116545556" style="display:none">A highly mixed blend of brief historical stories of the wars and atrocities and dictators in various Central and South American countries, bits of dream fragments, lyrical, almost poetic phrases, fable or wisdom teaching stories...a hard book to describe. I would find a few concepts that would please my ear or make me pause to reflect awhile on a lovely metaphor of wine and grapes and life and then find a stark contrast on the next page of an account of torture and execution of an artist followed by political commentary or a description of a calm beach coated in snow. It was that flow between horrors and joys, great violence and spirit and moments of compassion that was so discomfitting, as life can be. Still, while the book gave me much to think about, I can't honestly say I enjoyed it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8874391317116545556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_201011429" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/201011429" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4086173-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577214368p2/4086173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/201011429?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/4086173-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086173-mike?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201011429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5293831211711557241">“Each person shines with his or her own light. No two flames are alike. There are big flames and little flames, flames of every color. Some people’s flames are so still they don’t even flicker in the wind, while others have wild flames that fill the air with sparks. Some foolish flames neither burn nor shed light, but others blaze with life so fiercely that you can’t look at them without blinking, and if you approach you shine in the fire.”</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_450941925" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/450941925" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2204526-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1315842289p2/2204526.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/450941925?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/2204526-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer450941925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15342631974214958297">I read this for a creative writing class. It was difficult to determine how to read it because of the unique style, but after listening to a lecture by him I wish I would have read it more slowly. I enjoy the unique writing style, after trying it myself for the class I appreciate his talent. This book is wonderful in the way it is part reporting, part creative non-fiction with personal accounts. If I could read Spanish it would probably be a more enjoyable read as this is a translation. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_730136557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/730136557" />
    <a title="Jan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1580090-jan"><img alt="Jan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442493200p2/1580090.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/730136557?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jan" href="/user/show/1580090-jan">Jan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1580090-jan?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer730136557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3793303789324784264">Cedric Belfrage, who translated this book from the Spanish, appears as a character in it, and the book is dedicated to him. The couple of hundred chapters are flash fictions or prose poems that use the techniques of magical realism in an autobiography. If you loved Galeano's <i>Memorias del Fuego</i> trilogy (as I do), my guess is that you'll also love this slighter work. I use the comparative adjective advisedly, as Galeano's lesser work would be almost any other writer's masterpiece.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_730136557'><a id="like_count_review_730136557" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/730136557?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F9490.The_Book_of_Embraces">Like</a></span>

<div id="review_2853732823" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2853732823" />
    <a title="Cristiano Dalbem" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14179336-cristiano-dalbem"><img alt="Cristiano Dalbem" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594585247p2/14179336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2853732823?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristiano Dalbem" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristiano Dalbem" href="/user/show/14179336-cristiano-dalbem">Cristiano Dalbem</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788525414885" href="/book/show/32686334-o-livro-dos-abra-os">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2853732823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6651510893042686566">Some of its stories and quotes are among my favorite in literature. Still, most of the book was really hard to connect to since the characters and history behind the passages were unknown to me. Probably I'm more guilty here than the author, and I'm admitably not a connaisseur of Latin America history. Still, I'd like to have had a more relatable experience with such a book that didn't seem to need so much background knowledge to appreciate its sensitivity and clever beauty.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_178748534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178748534" />
    <a title="Elizabeth Andrew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3841375-elizabeth-andrew"><img alt="Elizabeth Andrew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442464469p2/3841375.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178748534?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth Andrew" href="/user/show/3841375-elizabeth-andrew">Elizabeth Andrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3841375-elizabeth-andrew?shelf=essays">essays</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178748534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4120863638889054836">A remarkable book for its structure and social commentary. Made up entirely of short anecdotes, THE BOOK OF EMBRACES is unified by voice (curmudgeonly, observant, funny) and by a sweeping critique of colonial culture, pop culture, dictatorships, and market-based economies. A thoughtful but quick read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aM2aQKCDFR644HTSVxyFUhvoAs6+tQ0z+BGCOlfoiup/afab4WvpE9jtZ9ltV9ti0zcfWW+6H+QRt4JMC7NwXA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('geE+/8X1ArBUipudyM9yVHfFe0dtrrXkV0gDibTP2geWRVIkhB3+vTSHiJbyhCxkvxpm0LyhpzO+7gP/6JQgsQ==')})
  }
//]]>

Daí que a resistência indígena se dê pela não aceitação da ideia de que somos todos iguais. Somente o reconhecimento da diversidade e a recusa da ideia do humano como superior aos demais seres podem ressignificar nossas existências e refrear nossa marcha insensata em direção ao abismo.\n\n&quot;Nosso tempo é especialista em produzir ausências: do sentido de viver em sociedade, do próprio sentido da experiência da vida. Isso gera uma intolerância muito grande com relação a quem ainda é capaz de experimentar o prazer de estar vivo, de dançar e de cantar. En este alucinante drama de la vida interior, seres intrincados en la bestial búsqueda de comprensión ceden a la mentira, la hipocresía y los celos desmedidos hasta el crimen más inexplicable. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7157682989766698884">Eduardo Galeano was a Uruguayan journalist, writer and novelist. His best known works are <i>Memoria del fuego</i> (Memory of Fire Trilogy, 1986) and <i>Las venas abiertas de América Latina</i> (Open Veins of Latin America, 1971) which have been translated into twenty languages and transcend orthodox genres: combining fiction, journalism, political analysis, and history. <br/><br/>The author himself has proclaimed his ob</span>
  <span id="freeText7157682989766698884" style="display:none">Eduardo Galeano was a Uruguayan journalist, writer and novelist. His best known works are <i>Memoria del fuego</i> (Memory of Fire Trilogy, 1986) and <i>Las venas abiertas de América Latina</i> (Open Veins of Latin America, 1971) which have been translated into twenty languages and transcend orthodox genres: combining fiction, journalism, political analysis, and history. <br /><br />The author himself has proclaimed his obsession as a writer saying, <i>"I'm a writer obsessed with remembering, with remembering the past of America above all and above all that of Latin America, intimate land condemned to amnesia."</i><br /><br />He has received the International Human Rights Award by Global Exchange (2006) and the Stig Dagerman Prize (2010).</span>
  <a data-text-id="7157682989766698884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
